\raisebox{\heightof{T}}[0pt][0pt]{\index{AV\_CODEC\_HW\_CONFIG\_METHOD\_HW\_FRAMES\_CTX@{AV\_CODEC\_HW\_CONFIG\_METHOD\_HW\_FRAMES\_CTX}!framesync.c@{framesync.c}}\index{framesync.c@{framesync.c}!AV\_CODEC\_HW\_CONFIG\_METHOD\_HW\_FRAMES\_CTX@{AV\_CODEC\_HW\_CONFIG\_METHOD\_HW\_FRAMES\_CTX}}}\mbox{\Hypertarget{framesync_8c_gga06fc87d81c62e9abb8790b6e5713c55ba5a73dc7ff24a0b8ed69e2673d026ca11}\label{framesync_8c_gga06fc87d81c62e9abb8790b6e5713c55ba5a73dc7ff24a0b8ed69e2673d026ca11}} 
A\+V\+\_\+\+C\+O\+D\+E\+C\+\_\+\+H\+W\+\_\+\+C\+O\+N\+F\+I\+G\+\_\+\+M\+E\+T\+H\+O\+D\+\_\+\+H\+W\+\_\+\+F\+R\+A\+M\+E\+S\+\_\+\+C\+TX&The codec supports this format via the hw\+\_\+frames\+\_\+ctx interface.

When selecting this format for a decoder, \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_a_v_codec_context_a3bac44bb0b016ab838780cc19ac277d6}{A\+V\+Codec\+Context.\+hw\+\_\+frames\+\_\+ctx}} should be set to a suitable frames context inside the \mbox{\hyperlink{doc_2examples_2qsvdec_8c_afe1023087c26d2d410c9cd7d491c8660}{get\+\_\+format()}} callback. The frames context must have been created on a device of the specified type.

When selecting this format for an encoder, \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_a_v_codec_context_a3bac44bb0b016ab838780cc19ac277d6}{A\+V\+Codec\+Context.\+hw\+\_\+frames\+\_\+ctx}} should be set to the context which will be used for the input frames before calling \mbox{\hyperlink{group__lavc__core_ga11f785a188d7d9df71621001465b0f1d}{avcodec\+\_\+open2()}}. \\

A\+V\+\_\+\+F\+R\+A\+M\+E\+\_\+\+C\+R\+O\+P\+\_\+\+U\+N\+A\+L\+I\+G\+N\+ED&Apply the maximum possible cropping, even if it requires setting the \mbox{\hyperlink{struct_a_v_frame_a1d0f65014a8d1bf78cec8cbed2304992}{A\+V\+Frame.\+data}}\mbox{[}\mbox{]} entries to unaligned pointers. Passing unaligned data to F\+Fmpeg A\+PI is generally not allowed, and causes undefined behavior (such as crashes). You can pass unaligned data only to F\+Fmpeg A\+P\+Is that are explicitly documented to accept it. Use this flag only if you absolutely know what you are doing. \\

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em f0} & used to return the main frame \\

{\em f1} & used to return the second frame, or N\+U\+LL if disabled \\

\index{framesync.c@{framesync.c}!ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput@{ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput}}
\index{ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput@{ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput}!framesync.c@{framesync.c}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput()}{ff\_framesync\_init\_dualinput()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{ffmpeg__filter_8c_a61569f2965b7a369eb10b6d75d410d11}{int}} ff\+\_\+framesync\+\_\+init\+\_\+dualinput (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_f_f_frame_sync}{F\+F\+Frame\+Sync}} $\ast$}]{fs,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_a_v_filter_context}{A\+V\+Filter\+Context}} $\ast$}]{parent }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Initialize a frame sync structure for dualinput.

Compared to generic framesync, dualinput assumes the first input is the main one and the filtering is performed on it. The first input will be the only one with sync set and generic timeline support will just pass it unchanged when disabled.

Equivalent to ff\+\_\+framesync\+\_\+init(fs, parent, 2) then setting the time base, sync and ext modes on the inputs.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ff\_framesync\_preinit()}{ff\_framesync\_preinit()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{rematrix__template_8c_a4dfdfbb7b69470f1152e022432ee2d45}{void}} ff\+\_\+framesync\+\_\+preinit (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{struct_f_f_frame_sync}{F\+F\+Frame\+Sync}} $\ast$}]{fs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Pre-\/initialize a frame sync structure.

It sets the class pointer and inits the options to their default values. The entire structure is expected to be already set to 0. This step is optional, but necessary to use the options.
